      <p>
       The
       <b>
        timeline of discovery of Solar System planets and their natural satellites
       </b>
       charts the progress of the discovery of new bodies over history. Each object is listed in chronological order of its discovery (multiple dates occur when the moments of imaging, observation, and publication differ), identified through its various designations (including temporary and permanent schemes), and the discoverer(s) listed.
      </p>
      <p>
       Historically the
       <a href="/wiki/Naming_of_moons" title="Naming of moons">
        naming of moons
       </a>
       did not always match the times of their discovery. Traditionally, the discoverer enjoys the privilege of naming the new object; however, some neglected to do so (
       <a href="/wiki/Edward_Emerson_Barnard" title="Edward Emerson Barnard">
        E. E. Barnard
       </a>
       stated he would "defer any suggestions as to a name" [for Amalthea] "until a later paper"
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barnard_1892_1-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Barnard_1892-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but never got around to picking one from the numerous suggestions he received) or actively declined (
       <a href="/wiki/Seth_Barnes_Nicholson" title="Seth Barnes Nicholson">
        S. B. Nicholson
       </a>
       stated "Many have asked what the new satellites" [Lysithea and Carme] "are to be named. They will be known only by the numbers X and XI, written in Roman numerals, and usually prefixed by the letter J to identify them with Jupiter."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nicholson_1939_2-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nicholson_1939-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ). The issue arose nearly as soon as planetary satellites were discovered: Galileo referred to the
       <a href="/wiki/Galilean_moons" title="Galilean moons">
        four main satellites of Jupiter
       </a>
       using numbers while the names suggested by his rival
       <a href="/wiki/Simon_Marius" title="Simon Marius">
        Simon Marius
       </a>
       gradually gained universal acceptance. The
       <a href="/wiki/International_Astronomical_Union" title="International Astronomical Union">
        International Astronomical Union
       </a>
       (IAU) eventually started officially approving names in the late 1970s.
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Key">
        Key
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_discovery_of_Solar_System_planets_and_their_moons&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Key">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       In the following tables, planetary satellites are indicated in bold type (e.g.
       <b>
        Moon
       </b>
       ) while planets and dwarf planets, which directly circle the Sun, are in italic type (e.g.
       <i>
        Earth
       </i>
       ). The tables are sorted by publication/announcement date. Dates are annotated with the following symbols:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <i>
         i:
        </i>
        for date of first imaging (photography, etc.);
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         o:
        </i>
        for date of first human visual observation, either through telescope or on photographic plate (the true discovery moment);
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         p:
        </i>
        for date of announcement or publication.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       In a few cases, the date is uncertain and is then marked "(?)".
      </p>
      <p>
       <i>
        * Note: Moons marked by an asterisk (*) had complicated discoveries. Some took years to be confirmed, and in several cases were actually lost and rediscovered. Others were found in
        <a href="/wiki/Voyager_program" title="Voyager program">
         Voyager
        </a>
        photographs years after they were taken.
       </i>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Color legend
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The planets and their natural satellites are marked in the following colors:
      </p>
      <div>
       <table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:500px;">
        <tr>
         <td style="width:50%; text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
          <dl>
           <dt>
            Planets
           </dt>
          </dl>
          <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
           <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid #AAAAAA; background-color: #D2B48C; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
           </span>
           <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(planet)" title="Mercury (planet)">
            Mercury
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
           <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid #AAAAAA; background-color: #98FB98; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
           </span>
           <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">
            Venus
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
           <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid #AAAAAA; background-color: #CCCC99; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
           </span>
           <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">
            Earth
           </a>
           and
           <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">
            satellite
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
           <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid #AAAAAA; background-color: #E9967A; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">

       </li>

        Permanent designations (of planetary satellites) are explained
        <a href="/wiki/Naming_of_moons#Roman_numeral_designations" title="Naming of moons">
         here
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Temporary designations are explained
        <a href="/wiki/Provisional_designation_in_astronomy#Satellites_and_rings_of_planets" title="Provisional designation in astronomy">
         here
        </a>

       </li>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">
        Prehistory
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_discovery_of_Solar_System_planets_and_their_moons&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Prehistory">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="wikitable" width="800">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="5" id="cPrehistory" style="background-color: Silver; text-align: center;">
         <a href="/wiki/Prehistory" title="Prehistory">
          Prehistory
         </a>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         Name
        </th>
        <th>
         Image
        </th>
        <th>
         Other designation
        </th>
        <th>
         Notes
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td bgcolor="#FFD700">
         <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">
          Sun
         </a>
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="black">
         <div class="center">
          <div class="floatnone">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sun_in_February.jpg">
            <img alt="Sun in February.jpg" data-file-height="2632" data-file-width="2632" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Sun_in_February.jpg/50px-Sun_in_February.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Sun_in_February.jpg/75px-Sun_in_February.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Sun_in_February.jpg/100px-Sun_in_February.jpg 2x" width="50"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="#FFD700">
         <i>
          Star
         </i>
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="#FFD700">
         In
         <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">
          Ptolemy
         </a>
         's
         <a href="/wiki/Geocentric_model" title="Geocentric model">
          geocentric model
         </a>
         , the Earth was believed to be at the center of the cosmos. Seven planets were placed in orbit around it in an order of increasing distance from the Earth, as established by the Greek
         <a href="/wiki/Stoicism" title="Stoicism">
          Stoics
         </a>
         : the Moon, Mercury, Venus, the Sun, Mars, Jupiter and Saturn. This list included two objects, the Sun and the Moon, which are no longer considered to be planets.
         <br/>
         <br/>
         <p>
          In the 5th century BCE the Greek philosophers
          <a href="/wiki/Philolaus" title="Philolaus">
           Philolaus
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Hicetas" title="Hicetas">
           Hicetas
          </a>
          speculated separately that the Earth was a sphere revolving daily around some mystical “central fire” that regulated the universe.
          <a href="/wiki/Anaxagoras" title="Anaxagoras">
           Anaxagoras
          </a>
          proposed that the Sun is a
          <a href="/wiki/Star" title="Star">
           star
          </a>
          around 450 BCE. In the 3rd century BCE, Aristarchus of Samos extended this idea by proposing that the Earth and other planets moved around a definite central object, which he believed to be the Sun though this was not widely accepted until the
          <a href="/wiki/17th_century" title="17th century">
           17th century
          </a>
          and not proven conclusively until the
          <a href="/wiki/19th_century" title="19th century">
           19th
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
           <a href="#cite_note-3">
            [3]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td bgcolor="#D2B48C">
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(planet)" title="Mercury (planet)">
           Mercury
          </a>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="black">
         <div class="center">
          <div class="floatnone">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mercury_as_Never_Seen_Before_(cropped).jpg">
            <img alt="Mercury as Never Seen Before (cropped).jpg" data-file-height="927" data-file-width="927" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Mercury_as_Never_Seen_Before_%28cropped%29.jpg/50px-Mercury_as_Never_Seen_Before_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Mercury_as_Never_Seen_Before_%28cropped%29.jpg/75px-Mercury_as_Never_Seen_Before_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Mercury_as_Never_Seen_Before_%28cropped%29.jpg/100px-Mercury_as_Never_Seen_Before_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="50"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="#D2B48C">
         <i>
          1st planet
         </i>
        </td>
        <td rowspan="6">
         The inner planets, Mercury and Venus, and the outer planets, Mars, Jupiter and Saturn, were identified by ancient
         <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_astronomy" title="Babylonian astronomy">
          Babylonian astronomers
         </a>
         in the 2nd millennium BC.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sachs_1974_4-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Sachs_1974-4">
           [4]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <p>
          By
          <a href="/wiki/Aristarchus_of_Samos" title="Aristarchus of Samos">
           Aristarchus of Samos
          </a>
          , and later in
          <a href="/wiki/Nicolaus_Copernicus" title="Nicolaus Copernicus">
           Nicolaus Copernicus
          </a>
          '
          <a href="/wiki/Heliocentrism" title="Heliocentrism">
           heliocentric system
          </a>
          (
          <i>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/De_Revolutionibus_Orbium_Coelestium" title="De Revolutionibus Orbium Coelestium">
            De Revolutionibus Orbium Coelestium
           </a>
          </i>
          , 1543), the Earth came to be considered a planet revolving with the other planets around the Sun, in the following order of distance from the Sun: Mercury, Venus, Earth, Mars, Jupiter, and Saturn. The Sun, now situated near the center of revolution, was no longer considered a planet.
         </p>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr bgcolor="#98FB98">
        <td>
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">
           Venus
          </a>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="black">
         <div class="center">
          <div class="floatnone">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Venus-real_color_(crop_tight).jpg">
            <img alt="Venus-real color (crop tight).jpg" data-file-height="464" data-file-width="464" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Venus-real_color_%28crop_tight%29.jpg/50px-Venus-real_color_%28crop_tight%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Venus-real_color_%28crop_tight%29.jpg/75px-Venus-real_color_%28crop_tight%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Venus-real_color_%28crop_tight%29.jpg/100px-Venus-real_color_%28crop_tight%29.jpg 2x" width="50"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          2nd planet
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr bgcolor="#CCCC99">
        <td>
         <i>

        </td>
        <td bgcolor="black">
         <div class="center">
          <div class="floatnone">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17_(cropped).jpg">
            <img alt="The Earth seen from Apollo 17 (cropped).jpg" data-file-height="2724" data-file-width="2726" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17_%28cropped%29.jpg/50px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17_%28cropped%29.jpg/75px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17_%28cropped%29.jpg/100px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="50"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="#CCCC99">
         <i>
          3rd planet
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td bgcolor="#E9967A">
         <i>

          </a>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="black">
         <div class="center">
          <div class="floatnone">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mars_23_aug_2003_hubble_(cropped).jpg">
            <img alt="Mars 23 aug 2003 hubble (cropped).jpg" data-file-height="1422" data-file-width="1422" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Mars_23_aug_2003_hubble_%28cropped%29.jpg/50px-Mars_23_aug_2003_hubble_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Mars_23_aug_2003_hubble_%28cropped%29.jpg/75px-Mars_23_aug_2003_hubble_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Mars_23_aug_2003_hubble_%28cropped%29.jpg/100px-Mars_23_aug_2003_hubble_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="50"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="#E9967A">
         <i>
          4th planet
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td bgcolor="#FFE8E8">
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">
           Jupiter
          </a>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="black">
         <div class="center">
          <div class="floatnone">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jupiter_in_true_color.jpg">
            <img alt="Jupiter in true color.jpg" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1117" height="48" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Jupiter_in_true_color.jpg/50px-Jupiter_in_true_color.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Jupiter_in_true_color.jpg/75px-Jupiter_in_true_color.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Jupiter_in_true_color.jpg/100px-Jupiter_in_true_color.jpg 2x" width="50"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="#FFE8E8">
         <i>
          5th planet
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td bgcolor="#FFFFCC">
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">
           Saturn
          </a>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="black">
         <div class="center">
          <div class="floatnone">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ringworld_Waiting_(cropped).jpg">
            <img alt="Ringworld Waiting (cropped).jpg" data-file-height="672" data-file-width="1686" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Ringworld_Waiting_%28cropped%29.jpg/100px-Ringworld_Waiting_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Ringworld_Waiting_%28cropped%29.jpg/150px-Ringworld_Waiting_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Ringworld_Waiting_%28cropped%29.jpg/200px-Ringworld_Waiting_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="100"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="#FFFFCC">
         <i>
          6th planet
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td bgcolor="#CCCC99">
         <b>
          <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">
           Moon
          </a>
         </b>
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="black">
         <div class="center">
          <div class="floatnone">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FullMoon2010_(cropped).jpg">
            <img alt="FullMoon2010 (cropped).jpg" data-file-height="2184" data-file-width="2202" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/FullMoon2010_%28cropped%29.jpg/50px-FullMoon2010_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/FullMoon2010_%28cropped%29.jpg/75px-FullMoon2010_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/FullMoon2010_%28cropped%29.jpg/100px-FullMoon2010_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="50"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="#CCCC99">
         Earth I
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="#CCCC99">
         In the Copernican system, the Moon was considered to be no longer a planet but a
         <a href="/wiki/Natural_satellite" title="Natural satellite">
          natural satellite
         </a>
         of the Earth, and was originally thought to be the only body in that system whose revolution was not centered on the Sun.
        </td>
       </tr>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="17th_century">
        17th century
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_discovery_of_Solar_System_planets_and_their_moons&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 17th century">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="wikitable" width="800">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="6" id="c17th" style="background-color: Silver; text-align: center;">
         17th century
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         Date
        </th>
        <th>
         Name
        </th>
        <th>
         Image
        </th>
        <th>
         Permanent designation
        </th>
        <th>
         Discoverer(s) and notes
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="5" id="a1610s" style="background-color: Silver; text-align: center;">
         1610s
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr bgcolor="#FFE8E8">
        <td rowspan="2" style="white-space: nowrap;">
         o: January 7, 1610
         <br/>
         p: March 13, 1610
        </td>
        <td>
         <b>
          <a href="/wiki/Ganymede_(moon)" title="Ganymede (moon)">
           Ganymede
          </a>
         </b>
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="black">
         <div class="center">
          <div class="floatnone">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ganymede_g1_true-edit1.jpg">
            <img alt="Ganymede g1 true-edit1.jpg" data-file-height="790" data-file-width="790" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Ganymede_g1_true-edit1.jpg/50px-Ganymede_g1_true-edit1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Ganymede_g1_true-edit1.jpg/75px-Ganymede_g1_true-edit1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Ganymede_g1_true-edit1.jpg/100px-Ganymede_g1_true-edit1.jpg 2x" width="50"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td>
         Jupiter III
        </td>
        <td rowspan="4">
         <a href="/wiki/Galileo_Galilei" title="Galileo Galilei">
          Galileo
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Galileo_1610_5-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Galileo_1610-5">
           [5]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drake_1981_6-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Drake_1981-6">
           [6]
          </a>
         </sup>
         discovered the
         <a href="/wiki/Galilean_moons" title="Galilean moons">
          Galilean moons
         </a>
         . These satellites were the first celestial objects that were confirmed to orbit an object other than the Sun or Earth. Galileo saw Io and Europa as a single point of light on January 7, 1610; they were seen as separate bodies the following night.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IAUMoonDiscoveries_7-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-IAUMoonDiscoveries-7">
           [7]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr bgcolor="#FFE8E8">
        <td>
         <b>
          <a href="/wiki/Callisto_(moon)" title="Callisto (moon)">
           Callisto
          </a>
         </b>
        </td>
        <td bgcolor="black">
         <div class="center">
          <div class="floatnone">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Callisto_(cropped).jpg">

         <a href="/wiki/Anagram" title="Anagram">

         </i>

         <i>

            <img alt="PIA18317-SaturnMoon-Tethys-Cassini-20150411.jpg" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1024" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/PIA18317-SaturnMoon-Tethys-Cassini-20150411.jpg/50px-PIA18317-SaturnMoon-Tethys-Cassini-20150411.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/PIA18317-SaturnMoon-Tethys-Cassini-20150411.jpg/75px-PIA18317-SaturnMoon-Tethys-Cassini-20150411.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/PIA18317-SaturnMoon-Tethys-Cassini-20150411.jpg/100px-PIA18317-SaturnMoon-Tethys-Cassini-20150411.jpg 2x" width="50"/>

        <td>
         Saturn III
         <br/>
         <small>
          <span class="nowrap">
           Saturn I (1686–1789)
          </span>
         </small>
        </td>
        <td rowspan="2">
         Cassini.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PhilTrans_1686_11-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-PhilTrans_1686-11">
           [11]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <p>
          Together with his previous two discoveries, Cassini named these satellites
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Sidera_Lodoicea" title="Sidera Lodoicea">
            Sidera Lodoicea
           </a>
          </i>
          . In his work
          <i>
           Kosmotheôros
          </i>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kosmotheoros_12-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-Kosmotheoros-12">
            [12]
           </a>
          </sup>
          (published posthumously in 1698), Christiaan Huygens relates "Jupiter you see has his four, and Saturn his five Moons about him, all plac’d in their Orbits."
         </p>
        </td>
       </tr>

         <a href="/wiki/Comet" title="Comet">

         </a>
         .

           </a>

        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Piazzi" title="Giuseppe Piazzi">
          Giuseppe Piazzi
         </a>
         . He first announced his discovery on January 24, 1801, in letters to fellow astronomers.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoskin_1992_19-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Hoskin_1992-19">
           [19]
          </a>
         </sup>

         <i>
          Monatliche Correspondenz
         </i>

                   </b>
                   / 106 km / 0.017 Earths
                  </small>
                 </li>
                </ul>
               </li>
              </ul>
             </div>
